								<a href="https://securelist.com/category/malware-descriptions/" class="c-tag c-tag--primary">Malware descriptions</a>
							</p>
														<h1 class="c-article__title">How the Necro Trojan infiltrated Google Play, again</h1>							<div class="c-article__info">
																<p class="c-article__headline u-hidden u-block@md">
									<a href="https://securelist.com/category/malware-descriptions/" class="c-tag c-tag--primary">Malware descriptions</a>
								</p>
																<p class="u-uppercase"><time datetime="2024-09-23T10:00:56+00:00">23 Sep 2024</time></p>
								<p class="c-article__reading u-ml-auto@md">
									<svg class="o-icon o-svg-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="https://securelist.com/wp-content/themes/securelist2020/assets/sprite/icons.svg#icon-hourglass"></use></svg> <span class="js-reading-time"></span> minute read								</p>
							</div>
						</header>

						<div class="c-article__wrapper">

							<div class="c-article__main">

													<img src="https://securelist.com/wp-content/themes/securelist2020/assets/images/icon/icon-categories--invert.svg" />

			<a  href="https://securelist.com/author/dmitrykalinin/" >
													<img src="https://securelist.com/wp-content/themes/securelist2020/assets/images/avatar-default/avatar_default_3.png">

											<div class="js-reading-content">
												<div class="c-wysiwyg">
													<h2 id="introduction">Introduction</h2>
<p>We sometimes come across modified applications when analyzing suspicious files. These are created in response to user requests for more customization options within the app or for new features that the official versions don&#8217;t have. Unfortunately, it&#8217;s not uncommon for popular mods to contain malware. This often happens because they&#8217;re distributed on unofficial websites that don&#8217;t have any moderation. For example, last year we found popular WhatsApp mods <a href="https://securelist.com/spyware-whatsapp-mod/110984/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">infected with CanesSpy</a> and distributed this way. Before that, we found ads for WhatsApp mods <a href="https://securelist.com/malicious-whatsapp-mod-distributed-through-legitimate-apps/107690/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">infected with the Triada Trojan dropper</a> in the popular Snaptube application. However, even official app stores can be infiltrated by infected apps. In 2019, we <a href="https://securelist.com/dropper-in-google-play/92496/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">discovered</a> the Necro dropper hidden within CamScanner, a widely used document scanning and processing app available on Google Play. At the time of the malware discovery, this app had been downloaded to more than 100 million devices worldwide. Sadly, history has repeated itself, and this time the Trojan authors exploited both distribution vectors: the new version of the multi-stage Necro loader infected both apps in Google Play and modified versions of Spotify, Minecraft, and other popular applications in unofficial sources.</p>
<p>Our conclusions in a nutshell:</p>
<ul>
<li>The new version of the Necro Trojan has infected various popular applications, including game mods, with some of them being available on Google Play at the time of writing this report. The combined audience of the latter exceeds 11 million Android devices.</li>
<li>The new version of the Necro loader, like most payloads it loads, has begun to use obfuscation to evade detection.</li>
<li>The loader, embedded in some applications, used steganography techniques to hide payloads.</li>
<li>The downloaded payloads, among other things, could display ads in invisible windows and interact with them, download and execute arbitrary DEX files, install applications it downloaded, open arbitrary links in invisible WebView windows and execute any JavaScript code in those, run a tunnel through the victim&#8217;s device, and potentially subscribe to paid services.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="how-necro-spreads">How Necro spreads</h2>
<h3 id="necro-loader-inside-a-spotify-mod">Necro loader inside a Spotify mod</h3>
<p>In late August 2024, our attention was drawn to a Spotify mod called Spotify Plus, version 18.9.40.5. At the time of writing this, the mod could be downloaded from <a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/spotiplus.xyz/?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______2314be7f09ac204a&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener">spotiplus[.]xyz</a> and several related sites that linked to it. The original website claimed that the mod was certified, safe, and contained numerous additional features not found in the official app. We decided to verify the claims about the application&#8217;s safety by downloading the latest version from this website (<a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/acb7a06803e6de85986ac49e9c9f69f1/results?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______d7b67b532e8a7586&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener">acb7a06803e6de85986ac49e9c9f69f1</a>) and analyzing it.</p>
<div id="attachment_113883" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151057/necro-1-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113883" class="size-large wp-image-113883" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151057/necro-1-en-ru-es-1024x792.png" alt="Site containing the Spotify mod" width="1024" height="792" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151057/necro-1-en-ru-es-1024x792.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151057/necro-1-en-ru-es-300x232.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151057/necro-1-en-ru-es-768x594.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151057/necro-1-en-ru-es-453x350.png 453w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151057/necro-1-en-ru-es-740x572.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151057/necro-1-en-ru-es-362x280.png 362w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151057/necro-1-en-ru-es-800x619.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151057/necro-1-en-ru-es.png 1262w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113883" class="wp-caption-text">Site containing the Spotify mod</p></div>
<p>The mod implements a custom Application subclass that initializes an SDK named adsrun in its 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bd0029741025" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">onCreate</span></span></span> method. This SDK is intended for integrating several advertising modules into the application: among other things, it initializes a module named Coral SDK. Upon activation, Coral SDK transmits a POST request to a designated command-and-control server. This request contains encrypted JSON data, specifically detailing the compromised device and the application hosting the module. The encryption method employed is a substitution cipher, where the substitution values are generated using a standard Java pseudo-random number generator seeded with a predefined constant. See an example of data sent by the module below.</p>
		<div id="crayon-67193f6332bd8523238367" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

</span><span class="crayon-s">"18.9.40.5"</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67193f6332bd8523238367-13"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>

				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
The C2 server returns a JSON response with an error code, encrypted with the same method. A value of 0 indicates successful execution. In this case, the response from the C2 will also contain an array of one object with a link to download the image in PNG format and associated metadata: name, MD5, version, and so on. Intriguingly, the downloaded file is termed &#8220;shellP&#8221;, suggesting it might be a condensed form of &#8220;shellPlugin&#8221;.</p>
		<div id="crayon-67193f6332bda765345309" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>

    "code": 0,

			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"code"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67193f6332bda765345309-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"result"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">100</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67193f6332bda765345309-7"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"url"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67193f6332bda765345309-10"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
Next, the module verifies the integrity of the downloaded image by calculating its MD5 hash and comparing it to the value received from the server. A payload is hidden in this image using steganography, which the module must extract and execute in the next step.</p>
<p>Coral SDK uses a very simple steganographic algorithm. If the MD5 check is successful, it extracts the contents of the PNG file — the pixel values in the ARGB channels — using standard Android tools. Then the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bdb628272367" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">getPixel</span></span></span> method returns a value whose least significant byte contains the blue channel of the image, and processing begins in the code.</p>
<div id="attachment_113884" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151109/necro-2-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113884" class="size-large wp-image-113884" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151109/necro-2-en-ru-es-1024x524.png" alt="Steganographic algorithm for payload extraction" width="1024" height="524" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151109/necro-2-en-ru-es-1024x524.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151109/necro-2-en-ru-es-300x154.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151109/necro-2-en-ru-es-768x393.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151109/necro-2-en-ru-es-684x350.png 684w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151109/necro-2-en-ru-es-740x379.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151109/necro-2-en-ru-es-547x280.png 547w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151109/necro-2-en-ru-es-800x409.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151109/necro-2-en-ru-es.png 1108w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113884" class="wp-caption-text">Steganographic algorithm for payload extraction</p></div>
<p>If we consider the blue channel of the image as a byte array of dimension 1, then the first four bytes of the image are the size of the encoded payload in Little Endian format (from the least significant byte to the most significant). Next, the payload of the specified size is recorded: this is a JAR file encoded with Base64, which is loaded after decoding via DexClassLoader. Coral SDK loads the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bdd579085886" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">sdk</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">fkgh</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">mvp</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">SdkEntry</span></span></span> class in a JAR file using the native library 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bde752842201" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">libcoral</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">so</span></span></span>. This library has been obfuscated using the OLLVM tool. The starting point, or entry point, for execution within the loaded class is the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bdf426686905" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">run</span></span></span> method.</p>
<div id="attachment_113885" style="width: 693px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151116/necro-3-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113885" class="size-full wp-image-113885" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151116/necro-3-en-ru-es.png" alt="Starting the payload" width="683" height="385" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151116/necro-3-en-ru-es.png 683w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151116/necro-3-en-ru-es-300x169.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151116/necro-3-en-ru-es-621x350.png 621w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151116/necro-3-en-ru-es-497x280.png 497w" sizes="(max-width: 683px) 100vw, 683px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113885" class="wp-caption-text">Starting the payload</p></div>
<p>Therefore, the security claims made about the application on the mod website can be considered false.</p>
<h3 id="popular-applications-in-google-play-are-infected-with-necro">Popular applications in Google Play are infected with Necro</h3>
<p>Having searched for the loader in our telemetry, we found other apps infected with Necro, including those available in Google Play at the time of writing this report. Their combined audience numbered more than 11 million Android devices.</p>
<div id="attachment_113886" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151132/necro-4-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113886" class="size-large wp-image-113886" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151132/necro-4-en-ru-es-1024x816.png" alt="Wuta Camera app in Google Play" width="1024" height="816" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151132/necro-4-en-ru-es-1024x816.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151132/necro-4-en-ru-es-300x239.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151132/necro-4-en-ru-es-768x612.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151132/necro-4-en-ru-es-439x350.png 439w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151132/necro-4-en-ru-es-740x590.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151132/necro-4-en-ru-es-351x280.png 351w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151132/necro-4-en-ru-es-800x638.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151132/necro-4-en-ru-es.png 1429w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113886" class="wp-caption-text">Wuta Camera app in Google Play</p></div>
<p>Our first find is the Wuta Camera app. Judging by its page in Google Play, it was downloaded at least 10 million times. According to our data, the Necro loader has been embedded in it starting from version 6.3.2.148. The latest version of the app at the time of collecting information, 6.3.6.148 (<a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/1cab7668817f6401eb094a6c8488a90c/results?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______38d3a36bbe0f8523&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener">1cab7668817f6401eb094a6c8488a90c</a>), which was available on Google Play, also had the Necro loader. We reported the presence of malicious code to Google Play, after which the loader was removed from the app in version 6.3.7.138.</p>
<div id="attachment_113887" style="width: 319px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151144/necro-5-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113887" class="size-full wp-image-113887" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151144/necro-5-en-ru-es.png" alt="Malicious loader in Wuta Camera" width="309" height="353" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151144/necro-5-en-ru-es.png 309w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151144/necro-5-en-ru-es-263x300.png 263w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151144/necro-5-en-ru-es-306x350.png 306w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151144/necro-5-en-ru-es-245x280.png 245w" sizes="(max-width: 309px) 100vw, 309px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113887" class="wp-caption-text">Malicious loader in Wuta Camera</p></div>
<p>The second infected app we found was Max Browser.</p>
<div id="attachment_113888" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151200/necro-6-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113888" class="size-large wp-image-113888" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151200/necro-6-en-ru-es-1024x745.png" alt="Max Browser app in Google Play" width="1024" height="745" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151200/necro-6-en-ru-es-1024x745.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151200/necro-6-en-ru-es-300x218.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151200/necro-6-en-ru-es-768x559.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151200/necro-6-en-ru-es-481x350.png 481w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151200/necro-6-en-ru-es-740x539.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151200/necro-6-en-ru-es-385x280.png 385w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151200/necro-6-en-ru-es-800x582.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151200/necro-6-en-ru-es.png 1326w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113888" class="wp-caption-text">Max Browser app in Google Play</p></div>
<p>This browser, according to Google Play, has been installed more than a million times and, starting with version 1.2.0, also contained the Necro loader. After we reported it, Google took down the infected app from their store.</p>
<div id="attachment_113889" style="width: 318px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151213/necro-7-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113889" class="size-full wp-image-113889" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151213/necro-7-en-ru-es.png" alt="Necro Trojan within Max Browser" width="308" height="420" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151213/necro-7-en-ru-es.png 308w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151213/necro-7-en-ru-es-220x300.png 220w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151213/necro-7-en-ru-es-257x350.png 257w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151213/necro-7-en-ru-es-205x280.png 205w" sizes="(max-width: 308px) 100vw, 308px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113889" class="wp-caption-text">Necro Trojan within Max Browser</p></div>
<h3 id="whatsapp-mods-with-the-necro-loader">WhatsApp mods with the Necro loader</h3>
<p>We also found WhatsApp mods containing the Necro loader (<a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/0898d1a6232699c7ee03dd5e58727ede/results?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______23db0cf342fa22d7&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener">0898d1a6232699c7ee03dd5e58727ede</a>) in unofficial sources. The infected application is distributed under the package name 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332be1200682780" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">com</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">leapzip</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">animatedstickers</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">maker</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">android</span></span></span>. Interestingly, there&#8217;s a legitimate app on Google Play with the exact same package name that isn&#8217;t a WhatsApp mod, but instead offers a collection of stickers for the messaging app.</p>
<p>The loader contained within the ad module in these applications functions somewhat differently from the sample described above. For instance, the code isn&#8217;t obfuscated at all but is protected by the SecAPK code protector. Additionally, the application uses Google&#8217;s Firebase Remote Config cloud service as a C2, storing information about files that need to be downloaded and executed.</p>
<div id="attachment_113890" style="width: 887px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151222/necro-8-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113890" class="size-full wp-image-113890" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151222/necro-8-en-ru-es.png" alt="Running the payload" width="877" height="368" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151222/necro-8-en-ru-es.png 877w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151222/necro-8-en-ru-es-300x126.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151222/necro-8-en-ru-es-768x322.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151222/necro-8-en-ru-es-834x350.png 834w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151222/necro-8-en-ru-es-740x311.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151222/necro-8-en-ru-es-667x280.png 667w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151222/necro-8-en-ru-es-800x336.png 800w" sizes="(max-width: 877px) 100vw, 877px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113890" class="wp-caption-text">Running the payload</p></div>
<p>While examining this loader, we discovered an interesting quirk: the malicious code within it has an 84% or 90% chance of execution. Initially, a random number between 0 and 99 is generated. Subsequently, based on the application package name, a threshold for malware execution is selected: the generated number must exceed either 9 or 15 for the loader to launch. If the number meets this criterion, a corresponding flag inhibiting loader operation is set to 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332be2134819478" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-t">false</span></span></span>, and the malicious functionality is executed.</p>
<div id="attachment_113891" style="width: 510px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151229/necro-9-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113891" class="size-full wp-image-113891" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151229/necro-9-en-ru-es.png" alt="The malicious functionality will be executed with a predetermined probability" width="500" height="152" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151229/necro-9-en-ru-es.png 500w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151229/necro-9-en-ru-es-300x91.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 500px) 100vw, 500px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113891" class="wp-caption-text">The malicious functionality will be executed with a predetermined probability</p></div>
<p>Intermediate payloads downloaded by this loader are not pre-encoded. The Trojan receives both the entry point information for the downloaded file and the download link from its C2 server. According to our data, one of the payloads (<a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/37404ff6ac229486a1de4b526dd9d9b6/results?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______9a1434b6f5e34783&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener">37404ff6ac229486a1de4b526dd9d9b6</a>) bore resemblance to a loader found in a modified version of Spotify, albeit with minor variations.</p>
<ul>
<li>The next-stage payload (shellPlugin) is loaded without the aid of native code.
<div id="attachment_113892" style="width: 892px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151239/necro-10-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113892" class="size-full wp-image-113892" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151239/necro-10-en-ru-es.png" alt="Loading shellPlugin" width="882" height="256" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151239/necro-10-en-ru-es.png 882w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151239/necro-10-en-ru-es-300x87.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151239/necro-10-en-ru-es-768x223.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151239/necro-10-en-ru-es-740x215.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151239/necro-10-en-ru-es-800x232.png 800w" sizes="(max-width: 882px) 100vw, 882px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113892" class="wp-caption-text">Loading shellPlugin</p></div></li>
<li>A different path is used for the POST request to the command-and-control server to retrieve shellPlugin information.</li>
<li>Instead of using the steganographic algorithm, shellPlugin is decoded with Base64.</li>
</ul>
<h3 id="other-infected-applications">Other infected applications</h3>
<p>This is not an exhaustive list of our findings. In addition to Spotify and WhatsApp mods, as well as apps in Google Play, we found infected game mods, including the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Minecraft;</li>
<li>Stumble Guys;</li>
<li>Car Parking Multiplayer;</li>
<li>Melon Sandbox.</li>
</ul>
<p>Given that various apps from multiple sources, including official ones, were found to be infected, we believe that the developers used an untrusted solution for ad integration. This led to a malicious loader appearing in the apps. Our security solutions detect it with the following verdicts:</p>
<ul>
<li>HEUR:Trojan-Downloader.AndroidOS.Necro.f;</li>
<li>HEUR:Trojan-Downloader.AndroidOS.Necro.h.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="the-necro-lifecycle-in-the-wild-how-the-payload-works">The Necro lifecycle in the wild: how the payload works</h2>
<p>During our research, we managed to obtain several samples of payloads that the loader subsequently executes. This particular payload (<a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/fa217ca023cda4f063399107f20bd123/results?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______4a2100842f920811&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener">fa217ca023cda4f063399107f20bd123</a>) exhibits several interesting characteristics that allow us to classify it as belonging to the Necro family:</p>
<ul>
<li>The loader obtains download information from the C2 domain bearsplay[.]com. According to our telemetry data, the domain has been contacted by Necro-family malware.</li>
<li>According to our data, the C2 domains that this file interacts with are also being used by the Necro and <a href="https://securelist.com/unkillable-xhelper-and-a-trojan-matryoshka/96487/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">xHelper</a> Trojans.</li>
<li>The functionality of this new payload is very similar to the previous version of Necro (<a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/402b91c6621b8093d44464fc006e706a/results?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______13feadddb0d878e7&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener">402b91c6621b8093d44464fc006e706a</a>). The code of the Trojans is also similar, but in this new payload, the attackers have used an obfuscator to make it harder for security solutions to detect and analyze.
<div id="attachment_113893" style="width: 707px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151247/necro-11-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113893" class="size-full wp-image-113893" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151247/necro-11-en-ru-es.png" alt="Code snippet from the payload" width="697" height="443" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151247/necro-11-en-ru-es.png 697w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151247/necro-11-en-ru-es-300x191.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151247/necro-11-en-ru-es-551x350.png 551w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151247/necro-11-en-ru-es-441x280.png 441w" sizes="(max-width: 697px) 100vw, 697px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113893" class="wp-caption-text">Code snippet from the payload</p></div>
<div id="attachment_113894" style="width: 660px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151255/necro-12-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113894" class="size-full wp-image-113894" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151255/necro-12-en-ru-es.png" alt="Similar code snippet from an old version of Necro" width="650" height="340" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151255/necro-12-en-ru-es.png 650w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151255/necro-12-en-ru-es-300x157.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151255/necro-12-en-ru-es-535x280.png 535w" sizes="(max-width: 650px) 100vw, 650px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113894" class="wp-caption-text">Similar code snippet from an old version of Necro</p></div></li>
<li>The payload configuration structure is identical to that of older versions of Necro, including the one we previously discovered in the CamScanner app. The field names in the configuration match the corresponding fields in other Necro versions.</li>
</ul>
<p>Based on this, we assert that both the examined payload and the original loader belong to the Necro family, which is familiar to us.</p>
<h3 id="payload-structure">Payload structure</h3>
<p>Now let&#8217;s move on to analyzing the payload. The second stage of the launch process reads a JSON-formatted configuration embedded within the code. An example of the configuration is provided below.</p>
		<div id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
{
    "hs":{
        "server":"https://oad1.azhituo.com:9190",
        "default":"https://oad1.azhituo.com:9190",
        "dataevent":"https://oad1.azhituo.com:9190",
        "PluginServer":"https://oad1.azhituo.com:9190"
    },
    "ps":{
        "web":"canna",
        "dsp":"hatch"
    },
    "mp":{
        "PMask":"159"
    },
    "rp":{}
}</textarea></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-6">6</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-7">7</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-8">8</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-9">9</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-10">10</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-11">11</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-12">12</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-13">13</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-14">14</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-15">15</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-16">16</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-1"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-2"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"hs"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"server"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-s">"https://oad1.azhituo.com:9190"</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"default"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-s">"https://oad1.azhituo.com:9190"</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-5"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"dataevent"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-s">"https://oad1.azhituo.com:9190"</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-6"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"PluginServer"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-s">"https://oad1.azhituo.com:9190"</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-7"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-8"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"ps"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-9"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"web"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-s">"canna"</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-10"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"dsp"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-s">"hatch"</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-11"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-12"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"mp"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-13"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"PMask"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-s">"159"</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-14"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-15"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-s">"rp"</span><span class="crayon-sy">:</span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67193f6332be4239957152-16"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
The 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332be5104120841" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">rp</span></span></span> switch might contain malicious services to be launched, but it was empty in the samples we analyzed.</p>
<div id="attachment_113895" style="width: 736px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151304/necro-13-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113895" class="size-full wp-image-113895" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151304/necro-13-en-ru-es.png" alt="Code for launching the malicious service from the &quot;rp&quot; parameter" width="726" height="628" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151304/necro-13-en-ru-es.png 726w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151304/necro-13-en-ru-es-300x260.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151304/necro-13-en-ru-es-405x350.png 405w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151304/necro-13-en-ru-es-324x280.png 324w" sizes="(max-width: 726px) 100vw, 726px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113895" class="wp-caption-text">Code for launching the malicious service from the &#8220;rp&#8221; parameter</p></div>
<p>The 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332be6744859455" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">mp</span></span></span> configuration switch holds parameters for the second-stage loader. It&#8217;s likely an abbreviation for &#8220;module parameters&#8221;.</p>
<p>The malicious functionality of Necro is implemented in additional modules that are downloaded from the C2 server. The malware authors frequently refer to these as &#8220;plugins&#8221; in the code. The 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332be7415925997" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">ps</span></span></span> configuration field (likely an abbreviation for &#8220;plugin stop list&#8221;, meaning a list of prohibited plugins) is necessary to block these modules. The switches in this object are the names of plugins that are forbidden to load, and the values are alternative plugins that can be executed instead of the blocked ones if they were loaded. The download ban will be applied if the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332be8925634646" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">mp</span></span></span> field has the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bea077038947" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">PluginControl</span></span></span> flag set to 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332beb643515720" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-t">true</span></span></span>. However, in the samples we were able to obtain, the restrictions did not apply. Additionally, the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bec676215691" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">mp</span></span></span> field may contain the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bed684444156" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">PluginUpdateFeature</span></span></span> flag, which controls plugin updates. If this flag is not present, plugins will be updated by default.</p>
<p>The 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bee341129902" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">hs</span></span></span> switch in the configuration stores a list of C2 addresses which the Trojan will talk to. Note that the malware logic does not require all addresses to match, although in the sample we examined, they were identical. The Trojan needs each address to perform the following tasks:</p>
<ul>
<li>
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bef691452577" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">server</span></span></span> is used to update the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bf1839738598" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">PluginServer</span></span></span> server address. To do this, the Trojan first sends a POST request containing the ID of the malicious implant and the name of the application package it&#8217;s embedded into. After that, the server can send a new 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bf2932539896" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">PluginServer</span></span></span> address. If the address cannot be updated, the value from the configuration set in the code is used.
<div id="attachment_113896" style="width: 695px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151315/necro-14-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113896" class="size-full wp-image-113896" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151315/necro-14-en-ru-es.png" alt="Updating PluginServer" width="685" height="304" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151315/necro-14-en-ru-es.png 685w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151315/necro-14-en-ru-es-300x133.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151315/necro-14-en-ru-es-631x280.png 631w" sizes="(max-width: 685px) 100vw, 685px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113896" class="wp-caption-text">Updating PluginServer</p></div></li>
<li>
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bf3605982581" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">dataevent</span></span></span> is used to store various events related to SDK activity.</li>
<li>
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bf4307026240" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-st">default</span></span></span> is not used at this stage.</li>
<li>
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bf5024474039" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">PluginServer</span></span></span> instructs the Trojan which plugins to download. Initially, a large amount of data is sent to this server. This includes information about the infected device (screen size, RAM, IMEI, IMSI, operating system version), information about the device&#8217;s environment (whether USB debugging mode and developer mode are enabled, if emulator artifacts are detected, etc.), details about the infected app, and so on.
<div id="attachment_113897" style="width: 667px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151323/necro-15-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113897" class="size-full wp-image-113897" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151323/necro-15-en-ru-es.png" alt="Sending collected data to PluginServer" width="657" height="339" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151323/necro-15-en-ru-es.png 657w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151323/necro-15-en-ru-es-300x155.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151323/necro-15-en-ru-es-543x280.png 543w" sizes="(max-width: 657px) 100vw, 657px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113897" class="wp-caption-text">Sending collected data to PluginServer</p></div></li>
</ul>
<p>In response, the server sends a list of plugins to download. These are downloaded asynchronously. To do this, the malware registers a broadcast receiver, and a separate thread, which is started for the download, sends a broadcast message when a plugin is ready to be downloaded. The plugins are differentiated by their name, which is also provided by the server.</p>
<h3 id="plugin-encryption-and-loading">Plugin encryption and loading</h3>
<p>The plugin loading code supports, among other things, the ability to decrypt plugins using various methods. Additionally, payloads can be extracted beforehand using the steganographic algorithm described above if a file with a .png extension was downloaded. The decryption method is specified in the file URL. The following options are available:</p>
<ul>
<li>
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bf6906879306" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-r">new</span></span></span>/
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bf7485441107" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">enc</span></span></span>: decryption with a substitution cipher similar to that used for C2 communication</li>
<li>
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bf9131333581" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">ssd</span></span></span>: plugin decryption using the DES algorithm</li>
<li>
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bfa366768453" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">ori</span></span></span>: unencrypted plugin
<div id="attachment_113898" style="width: 662px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151336/necro-16-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113898" class="size-full wp-image-113898" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151336/necro-16-en-ru-es.png" alt="Selecting a decryption procedure" width="652" height="478" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151336/necro-16-en-ru-es.png 652w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151336/necro-16-en-ru-es-300x220.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151336/necro-16-en-ru-es-477x350.png 477w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151336/necro-16-en-ru-es-382x280.png 382w" sizes="(max-width: 652px) 100vw, 652px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113898" class="wp-caption-text">Selecting a decryption procedure</p></div></li>
</ul>
<p>If no encryption method is specified, the plugin will be decrypted using a substitution cipher. The initial seed for this cipher will be the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bfb767439948" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">PMask</span></span></span> parameter (short for plugin mask), which is defined in the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bfc346715688" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">mp</span></span></span> object within the loader configuration. Once decoded, plugins can be loaded in various ways.</p>
<div id="attachment_113899" style="width: 626px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151345/necro-17-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113899" class="size-full wp-image-113899" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151345/necro-17-en-ru-es.png" alt="Selecting a method to load the plugin" width="616" height="891" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151345/necro-17-en-ru-es.png 616w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151345/necro-17-en-ru-es-207x300.png 207w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151345/necro-17-en-ru-es-242x350.png 242w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151345/necro-17-en-ru-es-194x280.png 194w" sizes="(max-width: 616px) 100vw, 616px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113899" class="wp-caption-text">Selecting a method to load the plugin</p></div>
<ul>
<li>
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bfd741329325" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">dex</span></span></span>: this method loads the plugin using DexClassLoader. The loader provides it with the application and plugin context, and additional plugin information.
<div id="attachment_113900" style="width: 776px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151358/necro-18-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113900" class="size-full wp-image-113900" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151358/necro-18-en-ru-es.png" alt="Loading the plugin in dex mode" width="766" height="548" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151358/necro-18-en-ru-es.png 766w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151358/necro-18-en-ru-es-300x215.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151358/necro-18-en-ru-es-489x350.png 489w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151358/necro-18-en-ru-es-740x529.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151358/necro-18-en-ru-es-391x280.png 391w" sizes="(max-width: 766px) 100vw, 766px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113900" class="wp-caption-text">Loading the plugin in dex mode</p></div>
<div id="attachment_113901" style="width: 711px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151411/necro-19-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113901" class="size-full wp-image-113901" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151411/necro-19-en-ru-es.png" alt="Launching the plugin entry point" width="701" height="454" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151411/necro-19-en-ru-es.png 701w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151411/necro-19-en-ru-es-300x194.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151411/necro-19-en-ru-es-540x350.png 540w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151411/necro-19-en-ru-es-432x280.png 432w" sizes="(max-width: 701px) 100vw, 701px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113901" class="wp-caption-text">Launching the plugin entry point</p></div></li>
<li>
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332bfe114586609" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">res</span></span></span>: this method allows loading plugins with new resources. These resources can be used to download more plugins in the future.
<div id="attachment_113902" style="width: 860px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151422/necro-20-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113902" class="size-full wp-image-113902" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151422/necro-20-en-ru-es.png" alt="Loading new resources" width="850" height="620" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151422/necro-20-en-ru-es.png 850w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151422/necro-20-en-ru-es-300x219.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151422/necro-20-en-ru-es-768x560.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151422/necro-20-en-ru-es-480x350.png 480w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151422/necro-20-en-ru-es-740x540.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151422/necro-20-en-ru-es-384x280.png 384w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151422/necro-20-en-ru-es-800x584.png 800w" sizes="(max-width: 850px) 100vw, 850px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113902" class="wp-caption-text">Loading new resources</p></div></li>
<li>
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332c00016018577" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">apk</span></span></span>: a method that allows sending information about a downloaded file to a service via the IPC Binder mechanism. The name of the service is specified in the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332c01230633084" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">bird_vm_msg_service</span></span></span> property. While it&#8217;s not definitively known which services Necro used, we can speculate that this function is used to install arbitrary APK files on the victim&#8217;s device.</li>
</ul>
<h3 id="types-of-plugins">Types of plugins</h3>
<p>To better understand the attackers&#8217; goals, we decided to thoroughly examine the payloads downloaded by the Trojan and, after analyzing telemetry data, found several Necro modules.</p>
<p><a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/ed6c6924201bc779d45f35ccf2e463bb/results?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______87161f48ec4f97be&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><strong>ed6c6924201bc779d45f35ccf2e463bb</strong></a><strong> – Trojan.AndroidOS.Necro.g</strong></p>
<p>This is a Necro module named &#8220;NProxy&#8221;. Its purpose is to create a tunnel through the victim&#8217;s device. When launched, the module connects to a server defined in the code.</p>
<div id="attachment_113903" style="width: 471px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151431/necro-21-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113903" class="size-full wp-image-113903" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151431/necro-21-en-ru-es.png" alt="Connecting to the server" width="461" height="109" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151431/necro-21-en-ru-es.png 461w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151431/necro-21-en-ru-es-300x71.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 461px) 100vw, 461px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113903" class="wp-caption-text">Connecting to the server</p></div>
<p>This server acts as a C2 server that the Trojan talks to via an unidentified protocol implemented over TCP sockets. The C2 sends commands, which the Trojan processes. After processing, the Trojan forwards traffic from one endpoint to another through the victim&#8217;s device.</p>
<p><a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/b3ba3749237793d2c06eaaf5263533f2/results?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______e835c58ab377f954&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><strong>b3ba3749237793d2c06eaaf5263533f2</strong></a><strong> – Trojan.AndroidOS.Necro.i</strong></p>
<p>We named this plugin &#8220;island&#8221;. When launched, the plugin generates a pseudo-random number, which it uses as an interval (in milliseconds) between displays of intrusive ads.</p>
<div id="attachment_113904" style="width: 882px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151441/necro-22-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113904" class="size-full wp-image-113904" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151441/necro-22-en-ru-es.png" alt="Trojan showing ads" width="872" height="676" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151441/necro-22-en-ru-es.png 872w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151441/necro-22-en-ru-es-300x233.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151441/necro-22-en-ru-es-768x595.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151441/necro-22-en-ru-es-451x350.png 451w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151441/necro-22-en-ru-es-740x574.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151441/necro-22-en-ru-es-361x280.png 361w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151441/necro-22-en-ru-es-800x620.png 800w" sizes="(max-width: 872px) 100vw, 872px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113904" class="wp-caption-text">Trojan showing ads</p></div>
<p><a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/ccde06a19ef586e0124b120db9bf802e/results?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______9161cf1e29f447ad&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><strong>ccde06a19ef586e0124b120db9bf802e</strong></a><strong> – Trojan.AndroidOS.Necro.d</strong></p>
<p>This plugin is named &#8220;web&#8221;, and it is one of the most popular Necro plugins, judging by our telemetry data. Its code contains a configuration similar in structure to the shellPlugin payload configuration in the previous stage. It&#8217;s interesting that the code for this plugin contains artifacts of older versions of Necro.</p>
<div id="attachment_113905" style="width: 554px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151447/necro-23-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113905" class="size-full wp-image-113905" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151447/necro-23-en-ru-es.png" alt="nicro is one such artifact from older Necro versions found within the plugin's configuration" width="544" height="315" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151447/necro-23-en-ru-es.png 544w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151447/necro-23-en-ru-es-300x174.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151447/necro-23-en-ru-es-484x280.png 484w" sizes="(max-width: 544px) 100vw, 544px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113905" class="wp-caption-text">nicro is one such artifact from older Necro versions found within the plugin&#8217;s configuration</p></div>
<p>Depending on the value of the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332c02575471849" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">CheckAbnormal</span></span></span> flag, the plugin checks for the presence of a debugger in the execution environment and if a phone is connected via USB using ADB. If either condition is met, the Trojan clears the Logcat log to hide traces of its activity. Additionally, the plugin verifies if it has the permission to display windows on top of other applications. After all these checks, it launches a malicious task that runs once every two hours. When the malware starts, it sends a POST request containing details about the infected device to the 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332c04439950105" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">server</span></span></span> server. This is done to get the address of another server, named 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332c05229113179" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-e">main </span><span class="crayon-i">URL</span></span></span>, which the Trojan will communicate with frequently. If there&#8217;s an error when getting this address, the malware will fall back to using a server named 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332c06347408268" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-st">default</span></span></span>.</p>
<div id="attachment_113906" style="width: 635px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151453/necro-24-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113906" class="size-full wp-image-113906" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151453/necro-24-en-ru-es.png" alt="Data about the infected device sent to the C2" width="625" height="232" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151453/necro-24-en-ru-es.png 625w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151453/necro-24-en-ru-es-300x111.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 625px) 100vw, 625px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113906" class="wp-caption-text">Data about the infected device sent to the C2</p></div>
<p>The received
