			<span id="crayon-67193f6332c07952638101" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-e">main </span><span class="crayon-i">URL</span></span></span> serves as the C2 server: it sends a list of pages to the Trojan, which the malware later opens in the background before processing the interactive elements contained on them. This functionality has a couple of interesting features. First, the Trojan code contains some artifacts that indicate it might be running with elevated privileges. However, Android processes with elevated privileges do not allow WebView by default. Privilege checks occur directly when creating an instance of the WebView factory: in privileged processes, it won&#8217;t be created. To circumvent this restriction, the Trojan creates an instance of the factory directly using reflection, thus bypassing all checks of the current process.</p>
<div id="attachment_113907" style="width: 657px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151507/necro-25-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113907" class="size-full wp-image-113907" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151507/necro-25-en-ru-es.png" alt="Instantiating a WebView factory directly" width="647" height="797" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151507/necro-25-en-ru-es.png 647w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151507/necro-25-en-ru-es-244x300.png 244w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151507/necro-25-en-ru-es-284x350.png 284w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151507/necro-25-en-ru-es-227x280.png 227w" sizes="(max-width: 647px) 100vw, 647px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113907" class="wp-caption-text">Instantiating a WebView factory directly</p></div>
<p>Secondly, the Trojan can download and run other executables, which are then used to replace links loaded with WebView. Combined with the functionality described above, this theoretically allows to do things like adding any additional information to the URL parameters of a replaced link, such as confirmation codes for paid subscriptions, as well as executing other arbitrary code when loading specific links.</p>
<p><a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/36ab434c54cce25d301f2a6f55241205/results?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______66631e855a9cdccb&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><strong>36ab434c54cce25d301f2a6f55241205</strong></a><strong> – Trojan-Downloader.AndroidOS.Necro.b</strong></p>
<p>This module is named &#8220;Happy SDK&#8221;. Its code partially combines the NProxy and web modules logic, as well as the functionality of the previous stage of the loader with a few minor differences:</p>
<ul>
<li>The code lacks the Trojan configuration, and backup C2 servers are located by default in the corresponding methods.
<div id="attachment_113908" style="width: 790px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151521/necro-26-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113908" class="size-full wp-image-113908" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151521/necro-26-en-ru-es.png" alt="Server address for updating the module is specified in the method code by default" width="780" height="496" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151521/necro-26-en-ru-es.png 780w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151521/necro-26-en-ru-es-300x191.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151521/necro-26-en-ru-es-768x488.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151521/necro-26-en-ru-es-550x350.png 550w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151521/necro-26-en-ru-es-740x471.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151521/necro-26-en-ru-es-440x280.png 440w" sizes="(max-width: 780px) 100vw, 780px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113908" class="wp-caption-text">Server address for updating the module is specified in the method code by default</p></div></li>
<li>The code corresponding to the &#8220;web&#8221; plugin lacks the functionality to execute arbitrary code.<br />
Note that we have occasionally encountered this SDK under the name &#8220;Jar SDK&#8221;. Analysis has shown that Jar SDK is a new version of Happy SDK.</p>
<div id="attachment_113909" style="width: 707px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151533/necro-27-en-ru-es.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113909" class="size-full wp-image-113909" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151533/necro-27-en-ru-es.png" alt="Happy SDK artifacts in Jar SDK" width="697" height="446" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151533/necro-27-en-ru-es.png 697w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151533/necro-27-en-ru-es-300x192.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151533/necro-27-en-ru-es-547x350.png 547w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151533/necro-27-en-ru-es-438x280.png 438w" sizes="(max-width: 697px) 100vw, 697px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113909" class="wp-caption-text">Happy SDK artifacts in Jar SDK</p></div></li>
</ul>
<p>We believe this is a different variant of Necro where the developers have opted for a non-modular architecture in the malicious SDK. This suggests that Necro is highly adaptable and can download different iterations of itself, perhaps to introduce new features.</p>
<p><a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/874418d3d1a761875ebc0f60f9573746/results?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______a6f82a7beac5a6e3&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><strong>874418d3d1a761875ebc0f60f9573746</strong></a><strong> – Trojan.AndroidOS.Necro.j</strong></p>
<p>We dubbed this plugin &#8220;Cube SDK&#8221;. It&#8217;s pretty simple and acts as a helper: its only job is to load other plugins to handle ads in the background.</p>
<p><a href="https://opentip.kaspersky.com/522d2e2adedc3eb11eb9c4b864ca0c7f/results?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______0a2df9cc21ac8c75&amp;utm_source=SL&amp;utm_medium=SL&amp;utm_campaign=SL" target="_blank" rel="noopener"><strong>522d2e2adedc3eb11eb9c4b864ca0c7f</strong></a><strong> – Trojan.AndroidOS.Necro.l</strong></p>
<p>This plugin, in addition to NProxy&#8217;s functionality, has an entry point for another plugin we&#8217;ve named &#8220;Tap&#8221;. Judging by its code, the latter is still under development: it contains a lot of unused functionality for interacting with ad pages. Tap downloads arbitrary JavaScript code and a WebView interface from the C2 server, which are responsible for viewing ads in the background. Among other things, the plugin includes 
			<span id="crayon-67193f6332c08530486313" class="crayon-syntax crayon-syntax-inline  crayon-theme-classic crayon-theme-classic-inline crayon-font-monaco" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important;"><span class="crayon-pre crayon-code" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;font-size: 12px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><span class="crayon-i">com</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">leapzip</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">animatedstickers</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">maker</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">android</span></span></span> as the package name of the infected app. This confirms that the WhatsApp mod loader described earlier, which uses Firebase Remote Config as a C2, also belongs to the Necro family.</p>
<p>These are all the payloads we were able to find during our research. For simplicity, we&#8217;ve combined all the processes described above into a single diagram illustrating all stages of the Necro Trojan.</p>
<div id="attachment_113910" style="width: 1034px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151551/necro-28-en.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-113910" class="size-large wp-image-113910" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151551/necro-28-en-1024x1013.png" alt="Necro Trojan infection diagram" width="1024" height="1013" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151551/necro-28-en-1024x1013.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151551/necro-28-en-300x297.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151551/necro-28-en-768x760.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151551/necro-28-en-1536x1520.png 1536w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151551/necro-28-en-354x350.png 354w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151551/necro-28-en-740x732.png 740w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151551/necro-28-en-283x280.png 283w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151551/necro-28-en-800x791.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151551/necro-28-en-50x50.png 50w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151551/necro-28-en.png 2048w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-113910" class="wp-caption-text">Necro Trojan infection diagram</p></div>
<p>It&#8217;s worth noting that the creators of Necro may regularly release new plugins and distribute them among infected devices, selectively or otherwise, for example, depending on the information about the infected application.</p>
<h2 id="victims">Victims</h2>
<p>According to Google Play data, the infected applications could have been downloaded over 11 million times. However, the actual number of infected devices might be much higher, considering that the Trojan also infiltrated modified versions of popular apps distributed through unofficial sources.</p>
<p>KSN data shows that our security solutions blocked over ten thousand Necro attacks worldwide between August 26th and September 15th. Russia, Brazil, and Vietnam experienced the highest number of attacks. The chart below illustrates the distribution of Necro attacks across countries and territories where users most frequently encountered the Trojan.</p>
<div class="js-infogram-embed" data-id="_/d8UUqIQtC2cMA9n46iZ3" data-type="interactive" data-title="01 EN countries-data" style="min-height:;"></div>
<p style="text-align: center;font-style: italic;font-weight: bold;margin-top: -10px"><em>Necro attacks by country and territory, August 26 through September 15, 2024 (<a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2024/09/19151610/necro-29-en.png" target="_blank" rel="noopener">download</a>)</em></p>
<h2 id="conclusion">Conclusion</h2>
<p>The Necro Trojan has once again managed to attack tens of thousands of devices worldwide. This new version is a multi-stage loader that used steganography to hide the second-stage payload, a very rare technique for mobile malware, as well as obfuscation to evade detection. The modular architecture gives the Trojan&#8217;s creators a wide range of options for both mass and targeted delivery of loader updates or new malicious modules depending on the infected application. To avoid being infected with this malware:</p>
<ul>
<li>If you have any of the aforementioned Google Play apps installed and the versions are infected, update the app to a version where the malicious code has been removed, or delete it.</li>
<li>Download applications from official sources only. Applications installed from unofficial platforms may contain malicious functionality.</li>
<li>Use a <a href="https://www.kaspersky.com/premium?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2c_securelist_lnk_sm-team___kprem____b9c5c8f2f87093c7" target="_blank" rel="noopener">reliable security solution</a> to protect your device from attempts to install malware.</li>
</ul>

					<div class="comment-reply"><a rel='nofollow' class='comment-reply-link' href='https://securelist.com/necro-trojan-is-back-on-google-play/113881/?replytocom=3566058#respond' data-commentid="3566058" data-postid="113881" data-belowelement="comment-3566058" data-respondelement="respond" data-replyto="Reply to Valerie Mullen" aria-label='Reply to Valerie Mullen'>Reply</a></div><!-- .comment-reply -->				</div><!-- .comment-content -->

		<li class="comment odd alt depth-2 " id="comment-3566127">
			<article>
				<figure class="comment-avatar">
									</figure>

				<header class="comment-header">
					<div class="comment-author">
						<p class="comment-name"><span>Dmitry Kalinin</span> <span class="says"></span></p>
						<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">

							Posted on							<time datetime="2024-09-30T12:54:52+00:00">September 30, 2024. 12:54 pm</time>						</div><!-- .comment-meta -->

					</div><!-- .comment-author -->
				</header>

				<div class="comment-content">
										<p>Hi Valerie!<br />
If your device runs one of the recent Android versions (10 or higher), you can do the following:<br />
If you have installed one of the modifications described in this article, you can simply delete it. The persistence mechanisms will be disabled and deleted from your device. Several plugins may remain in the storage, but it&#8217;s safe since they can&#8217;t be activated without the loader.<br />
If you have installed one of the applications from Google Play, please check its version. If it is yet unpatched or deleted from the store, delete the app. If an update is available, download and install it. Once you do, you can continue using the app as you would normally do.<br />
Your emails and text messages aren&#8217;t infected, and it&#8217;s safe to use your phone as per usual.<br />
However, if the device runs an outdated Android version, it allows the attackers to download root exploits, so it would be impossible to remove the malware safely. If that is the case, reflashing the device will help.<br />
Safe browsing!</p>
